Chapter XIX.
On the cauterization of a fistula in the mouth.
If in the root of the uvula or in the palate or in the roots of the teeth a pustule is formed and a boil is made, and it breaks, and it becomes old, and it makes a fistula, and you treat it and your treatment is not successful, then it is necessary that you ignite a cauterizing instrument according to the quantity received in the fistula, and then place the ignited tool in the fistula hole, and with your hand bring it to the root of him, and at the end do this once or twice; and treat it with what I have said about treatment until it is healed.
And so if the pus is drained and healed, that is good; otherwise, it is necessary to expose the location and scrape the rotten bone according to its chapter.
Chapter XX.
Treatment of cauterization of teeth and softening of ulcers.
When ulcers are softened by moisture and teeth are damaged, and you cannot heal them with medicine, then place the patient's head on your lap, bring the cautery near that is suitable for this purpose, ensure the patient can feel the heat of the fire reaching the root of the tooth.
Then lift your hand, and move the heated cautery several times according to your will.
Then the patient rinses their mouth with salt water and holds it for an hour, then stop it because the damaged tooth is closed, the swollen gum is tightened, and the corrupt moisture is dried up.
Chapter XXI.
Treatment of tooth pain by cauterization.
When tooth pain is caused by inflammation or worms, or medicine does not heal it, then cauterize the area in two ways: either with a cowhorn cautery, or with fire.
A cowhorn cautery is obtained by taking a cow's horn and heating it in an iron pot, then selecting a small piece of the heated horn and wrapping it in linen cloth, immersing it in water, and placing it on the painful tooth quickly until it becomes hot.
Then move the heated horn cautery several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth.
If you wish, immerse linen or a piece of cloth in the hot horn cautery, place it on the painful tooth, and hold it there until the heated iron reaches the cavity of the tooth.
However, the cauterization by fire method has the drawback that you must be careful with the coal or iron, and there should not be any large protrusions in the area to prevent the heat of the fire from reaching the patient's mouth.
Then heat the cautery in a suitable manner, and place it on the tooth until it becomes hot, and do this several times as needed to alleviate the pain either that day or the next.
And it is necessary to use pressure on the cautery so that the patient holds their mouth open with a good bite and keeps it there for an hour, then spit it out. This is the method of using the cauterization.
Cauterize only the affected area as much as is possible for you.
This is the shape of the cannula (a hollow tube used for medical procedures):
Chapter XXII.
Treatment of hernias by cauterization.
When hernias are caused by inflammation and cold humors that do not respond to medicine and you want to treat them gently, then heat the cautery in a suitable manner (as described below), holding both ends so that the smoke escapes through one end, and apply the heated cauterizer to the abscess for a moment. If necessary, repeat this process until it reaches the base of the abscess.
If the abscess is small, then pause the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and apply the linen for three days on it, and pause over the affected area until the fluid inside has been completely burned by the fire.
Approach it with warm cloths and bandages until it is healed.
Chapter XXIII.
On the cauterization of throat warts and constriction of veins.
When humidity comes upon the trachea of the lung, and especially when it is accompanied by inflammation, it is necessary that the patient be evacuated at first with laxative medicines, and then cauterize that affected place at the location of the goiter.
And be careful not to burn the goiter with the cautery or burn its surrounding tissue, but only a little.
Cauterize that affected place at another joint of the neck on the lower spine. The cautery used should be sharp, following the previous method.
Approach it with the warm cloths and bandages until it is healed.
Chapter XXIV.
On the cauterization of lung disease and cough.
When cough and lung disease are due to humidity, the patient does not have a fever or thick phlegm, and it is an old sickness, then cauterize that affected place with two cauteries on the furcula at the tender spots on both sides; and with another cautery in the middle of the thigh between two nipples; and let the cauteries be sharp, following the previously described method.
And if you wish, your cauterization can be made with the type of cautery called a punctum, which is described in the treatment of ear pain.
And place points at those areas; and approach it with warm cloths and bandages until it is healed.
And let the cauteries have three arms, since cauterization is done with this method: once a day you can perform three cauterizations in this manner.
Chapter XXV.
On the cauterization of twitching, which is the head of the assistant.
When the head of the assistant is displaced due to lubricating humidity and does not return to its place during the time of its return, then you must bring it back until it has returned to its usual position, and you must gently move it so that it can be dislocated in the opposite direction, as we have witnessed, then you should first reduce the displacement, and place the patient on their back or on their side; and raise the surrounding tissue which is inside the area of the twitching to the upper parts with your left hand if the joint is displaced internally.
Approach with fire the cautery that has two heads, and this is its shape:
Approach and cauterize the surrounding tissue so that it penetrates through to the other side, and the figure of cauterization will then come out with four heads.
And adjust it according to this count and because there are eight cauteries.
And pause over the cautery for a time with salt, and place the patient in quietness, and let the affected limb not be painful for any length of time until it is comforted.
And if the displacement is at the upper joint and the humidity is removed as described earlier, then you cauterize over the muscle with a sharp cautery or multiple pointed cauteries, since the joint is confirmed and the humidity is drained and the patient is healed.
Chapter XXVI.
On the cauterization of the stomach.
When there is movement and humidity in the stomach that spreads throughout its expanse and multiplies its rooms, and if you continue with the methods of treatment but it does not improve, then you must place the patient on their back, extend their arms and legs, and approach with three cauteries: one cautery below the thigh at the thickness of a finger, and two cauterize below the ribs of the caution, until the triangle-shaped figure of the cautery appears; and elongate those that are not aligned to produce an opening.
And if the depth of the cautery is two thirds of the thickness of the surrounding tissue.

On Perforation of Foot Apostema with Cautery (Title)
When an abscess or apostema arises in the foot and you want to know if that apostema is in the flesh of the foot or in its sheath (tunica), then if it is in the flesh of the foot, the patient feels heaviness and pain without being aggravated.
If it is in the sheath (tunica) of the foot, pain becomes intense and often exhausts doctors treating it.
Therefore, it is necessary that the patient lies on their back; and show the location of the abscess with a finger (or other pointing instrument); and ignite the cautery, similar to a rag, in the form described in the previous page. Cauterize with that and cauterize the abscess until the entire wound is burned (coagulated), until it reaches the cavity, until pus comes out.
And care for it with the treatment of other abscesses until healed.
It is not necessary to use this type of cautery unless it has been studied in the art of medicine for a long time and in which many diseases have been known; however, it is better to learn about this operation by trying it several times, but do not neglect it, and it is best.

And it's not necessary to close your hand around the cautery, rather let it be in the open during the operation.

Chapter 30.
On the cauterization of the liver.
When treating liver disease with the methods we have mentioned for division, do not use your own method, rather cauterize in that area according to three ways, all of which are permissible, of which one is to make three or four stitches along the length of the liver according to the figure of the cauteries in the foot, whose figure has been previously described.
And the thickness between each cauterization should be the size of a finger or slightly more, and the method of cauterization should be the same as the method we mentioned in the cautery of the foot.
And do not close your hand around the cautery; rather, let the patient lie on their back.
And another method of cauterization is to ignite the cautery with two prongs, as we have mentioned in the chapter on dislocation of muscles, and lift the skin that is at the end of the liver so that the patient can lie on their left side.
And your elevation should be such that you lift the skin according to the length of the body, so that cauterizations can be made according to the width of the body.
And bring the two prongs together, ignite them quickly, and penetrate the skin of the other part at that point.
And remove the cautery; therefore four cauterizations are made.
And if you wish, cauterize with a cautery having three prongs.
And take care to cure the cautery as it has been said to soak it in vinegar for several days, because that is more effective than the other causes mentioned in the treatment.
Chapter 31.
On the cauterization of hydropisis.
Cauterize not in hydropisis, but in an artery properly.
When treating hydropisis with the methods we have mentioned for division and you do not use your own method, it is necessary to cauterize with four cauterizations around the navel, one cautery on the stomach, another cautery on the foot, another cautery on the liver, two cauterizations between the vertebrae of the back, and a cautery in the center of the leg, and another cautery on the stomach. And the depth of the cautery should be appropriate for the thickness of the skin.
And let the cautery be soaked in vinegar so that it can be used for a long time.
And do not evacuate the patient from treatment with the cautery without those things that are necessary for healing, and rather hasten it with assistance.
The shape of the cautery used to treat the abdomen should be as described before, and it is that one which is used to treat the back, according to its previous shape.
Chapter .xxxii.
On the cauterization of feet and on sores.
When the feet are swollen with edema and filled with stagnant water, it is necessary to cauterize the feet on the back of the heel at the point between the little toe and the big toe, and lift your hand off the cautery and do not twist it; and raise your hand, and do not return it completely, because the stagnant water runs out.
The cautery is made in this way: Place two cauteries on each sore, and in each sore make a cautery with the tip of the cautery knife. Make the cauteries in accordance with the length of the sore: Place one on the left side and the other below the middle of the sore; and on each sore two cauteries.
When the wound remains open for a long time because some water persists in it.
And take care of those causes that we have mentioned.
Chapter .xxxiii.
On the cauterization of abdominal organs.
When an abdominal organ becomes weakened and humidity enters it, causing its digestive and retentive functions to weaken, which are in the stomach and the intestines, it is treated with various methods of treatment but does not improve, and sometimes the patient suffers from cauterization with a strong cautery, then cauterize that area with a large cautery on the stomach as described in the cauterization of the stomach, with a circular cautery and four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a sharp cautery; and with a cautery on the incision on the side of a large alkatin or with two cauteries.
And if excessive humidity persists and the patient tolerates it, then cauterize that area on the pelvis and intestines, and apply two strong cauteries to the stomach near the inguinal region, because this is a perfect cure for the problem, without any error.
Chapter .xxxiv.
On the cauterization of ancient hemorrhoids.
When ancient hemorrhoids are caused by nature or thick humors or decayed humidity, and are not cured with the methods mentioned in the division, then cauterize it with three cauteries on the tip of the coccyx at the base of the small triangle, and with a cautery above the navel through both sides.

On the cauterization of nails and other similar things.

Place your hand on the burning cautery over the clawfoot, and move your hand around the clawfoot with the cautery until it reaches the depth of the clawfoot. If it does not heal, and motes continue to develop on the surface of the body, especially on the back and feet, you must administer cauterization with hot water in these cases; take a cup made of glass or iron or a bird's beak, and place it on the clawfoot; then pour a small amount of hot water into the cup, hold your hand over it, and rotate the cup around the clawfoot with compression of your hand from all sides, pressing against the edge of the cup at the root of the clawfoot, allowing the hot water to flow into the root of the claw; wait for an hour for the patient to feel the heat of the hot water on the affected area, and then remove it, as the clawfoot with its roots will be eradicated.
And do this to all such cases until they are healed completely.
Treat the pus that arises when the roots of the claws are eradicated with general flesh-producing medication.

Chapter LVI.
On cauterization of blood flux due to sudden wound by incision of an arrow.
At certain intervals (after the arrow wound has been incised), the flux of blood is stopped by pressing down on the wound itself, or by the incision of an abscess or cauterization of the member, and in such a case, it often remains difficult to heal.
Therefore, whenever it happens (to stop the blood flux due to an arrow wound), you should press your thumb on the opening of the arrow, and wait for a certain number of intervals until the bleeding stops by itself, and does not come out again.
Then wait for the olive oil cauterizers (cautery sticks) to become hot and burn slightly, by counting a certain number of breaths, and blow on them until they are heated enough.

And if the blood is expelled from the opening of the artery when you press it and withdraw the cautery, then take another cautery from among those that have been prepared in the fire, and continue to perform this procedure until the blood has been constricted.
And be careful not to burn the nerves that are nearby, and let another person approach the patient with evil intentions.

But one who administers proper compression with a bandage or by placing hot substances and similar causes should not be trusted.

And this is the shape of the tool used to treat abscesses in wounds when seen, and it resembles a pair of forceps like those sometimes, but with some curvature: The handle should be placed in the wound, and the end of it is shaped like the beak of a stork, which is hollow, sharpened with a file, so that when any cause is compressed, it does not release.
Chapter XL.
This is the summary of the sermon on the topic of abscesses and their treatment.
Abscesses are various species, of multiple types, as remembered from them in this book.
And they are different in their penetration and excision of them by two methods, one of which is for abscesses that grow within themselves; and because of the humidity.
The second method is for locations where accidents of the body occur, as an abscess that occurs in the head is different from one that occurs in the anus; and an abscess in a fleshly location is different from one at a joint. And each of these has its own treatment through operation.
However, some abscesses should not be perforated except for the maturation of the pus or completion of their course.
Other abscesses that should be drained when they are hard, and not allowed to mature according to their course, include those near joints, as an abscess near a joint will continue to grow until the surrounding tissue is purged or the nerves of that joint are corrupted, which can cause contraction of the affected limb; or an abscess in a main organ, and if you delay the draining of it for too long, it can spread to the main organ; or one in the anus, therefore drain it before it matures; and it is not necessary to drain a hard abscess from the digestive tract, but rather the one that is in the anus, as it may cause prolonged pain if left untreated and could lead to a fistula or abscess near the anus that does not heal. You must know the time of the abscess's perforation, and that is when it has matured.
When the pain subsides and the fever ceases, when there is a reduction in swelling and pulse, when the abscess's head becomes more acute and other symptoms appear, then it is time for incision.
And know that the perforation should be made at a spot below the abscess, and from where pus is coming out for treatment of the prominence.
The perforation should be made along the flesh or body if abscesses are in the groin or feet and at the joints of the limbs, cords of nerves, arteries; and finally, in all places where there is no reflection; because in those that are reflected, use perforation according to that member.
When the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to wait for confirmation of its digestion before perforating, as we have said; because if you perforate too soon, you prolong the course of the pus and move it, and harden the edges and deepen the cavity.
Some abscesses should be perforated according to the thickness of the flesh or body as needed, or according to what that member requires.
You must make a small perforation in small abscesses and a large and wide or multiple incisions according to the size of the abscess.
Some abscesses that require the cavity to be concave and incised are done in such a way that they appear like bread and butter or when they are ripe, as in cases of tumors and buboes.
Of those that are incised and have three corners; and of these is the one that is incised like a myrtle leaf figure, as in the abscesses of gout.
And of those that are given round and crescent-shaped incisions, similar to these.
But in the case of superficial abscesses that do not have a specific form, you should perforate it with a surface or flat perforation only.
When the abscess is large and has collected pus, you must perforate it but do not rush to extract all the pus at that time; after extracting part of it, leave the abscess inside for another day, and then extract a larger part, and perform multiple observances according to gradation until it is forgotten.
Furthermore, if the patient is old, weak or a woman in labor, or a young child, then the animal spirit can be resolved with the exit of pus, and the patient may die as a result, so you should be careful with them.
Be very careful with this chapter and your perforation of these abscesses, as you must avoid wounds and consider whether the abscess wound is small or a flat incision; in such cases, administer one or two antiseptics; but if the abscess is large and the incisions are many, then you must wait for each to heal before proceeding.
And if in the abscess part of the cavity is removed or you have concaved it around its circumference, then you must seal it with old cote or thread made from cloth, like when you dress wounds or bandages, without moisture; and let it heal for three days; and process and cure it with the same care as for wounds until it heals.
But if bleeding occurs during the operation, administer cold water and wine diluted in linen cloth, and let it rest on the site of the bleeding for a while.
But if the bleeding persists, you must administer treatment and cure and powder as I have recommended in various places of this book and elsewhere.
If it is winter and the location of the abscess is near nerves, then you must apply powder in wine and warm oil and let it rest on those areas.
If it is summer and the areas are fleshy, then you must let the powder sit in water and oil or wine and oil, and let it rest until the third day as we have said, and then remove the abscess and clean it and administer to its cure whatever is appropriate for it until it heals.
And this is what is necessary for the knowledge of the treatment of abscesses in general, but according to the different methods of treatment that I have previously described for each type of abscess in specific chapters.

On incisions of abscesses that occur by arrow or vein.

And that which is due to a vein is rounded at the manifestation of the chest.

Chapter I: Abscess due to twisting of nerves.
Just as an abscess may occur in an arrow wound or vein, and similarly an abscess may occur in nerves when it occurs due to a blow or excessive labor, and so on.
It is most often found in the areas of the joints or ankles, or in any place where the joints are injured.
It is a serious abscess, and it resembles the color of the other body, and it is located in the larger areas that are swollen due to its pressure; and when the patient feels the pain, it appears like stupor.
It is not an abscess that runs along the front of the chest, and therefore, it does not have a sheath; it is damaged in all areas and does not extend towards the front or back.
Therefore, it is not necessary for those suffering in the joints to be wrapped with iron, because great cold will inevitably follow contraction.
However, one who has a headache or pain in the forehead is treated with spittle (saliva). If it is a small abscess, then you should use forceps and drain it.
If it is big, you should suspend it with unguent (ointment), excise it, and apply a dressing to it; then sew up the wound, and cure it until it is healed.

Chapter 2.
On the treatment of the navel in a prominent way.
The navel is treated for various reasons: either due to fissures on the abdomen, from which tissues or intestines protrude as in other ruptures; or by blood flowing from a vein or artery as previously mentioned, or by compressed bowel wind.
But if it is due to abdominal fissure and the protrusion of tissue, then the appearance of the boil is similar to that of the body; and it is lion-like in pain, and it appears in various ways. If it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then you must place it in the position where it had been previously retracted with much greater diversity; and when you press it with your fingers, it becomes hidden, and return it; and strong pressure is needed there, and it must be introduced with forceful bathing and vigorous effort.
But if it is due to moisture, then it does not become hidden when you press with your hand, nor is it compressed, nor is it painful.
And if it is due to blood, then the boil appears black and darkening in color.
But if it is due to rotten flesh, then the boil is heavy, large and hard, and it becomes filled up to a certain quantity.
And if it is due to wind, then the touch of it is painful.
The operation in this case is to consider whether the swelling of the navel is due to blood from an artery or vein, or wind; and if it is, you must refrain from treating it, because in such cases there is fear and dread, as taught in the chapter where abscesses from arteries and veins have been discussed.
And if the swelling of the navel is due to intestine or tissue, you must order the patient to lie on their back and remain extended; then hold the patient's abdomen taut in a circle around the entire navel, and order them to remain facing upwards between your hands; then surround the navel with a thin piece of cloth around the area that you have marked with the tension; and extend the size of the boil at the incision lines until it is very large; and tie it in the circle with strong thread or cord, taking care to make the tying method proper.
Then you cut the boil's incision across the middle and insert your finger into it to search for intestine; if you have not found or secured it with the ligament, then you extract any excrement and force the intestine back into the abdomen.

But that which is caused by inflammation of a vein cannot be dispersed by any means due to pressure with fingers.
And it is possible that on this type surgery may be performed and on other flesh; and you should make an incision in the genitals, place your fingers at the junctions above, and extract that from the white cavity, and release the suspenders of the vessels, tie them up, and make an incision where you have released it from all parts of the junction of the fingers.
Therefore, if the cavity is already consolidated with those flesh parts, you must then extract the cavity and incise it.
And if there is adhesion due to any cause within the cavity, or between the vessels, you must then release all that adhesion and incise it with a circular incision.
But if it is native flesh in the location of the adhesion which is behind, you must then incise all that which is there and extract the cavity as previously stated.
Therefore, when your operation is complete, fill the wound with wool soaked in oil and wine, and take care of it with other care until it heals.
Chapter LXIV.

Acute abscess is an abscess enveloped by some envelop like a bulb with softening of the testicles, and it makes difficult exercise and walking for the patient.

Chapter LXV.
On the cure of intestinal hernia.
The onset of this hernia is due to a section that extends in the cavity extended over the abdomen from the sides of the mirror of the abdomen, so that the intestines protrude through one of its junctions.
This rupture is either of the cavity or of the extension of it, and this happens due to various causes: impact, sneezing, shouting, lifting a heavy load, or something similar.
The sign of this, when it is due to extension of the cavity, is that it occurs gradually over a long time and does not occur suddenly, and it becomes an abscess in the groin because the cavity presses the intestine.
The sign of this is when it is due to a section of the cavity, because at the beginning it causes violent pain suddenly; and the abscess appears different from the proximate apparent one, and that is precisely the intestine, and the body of it outside the junction of the cavity.
Some occurrences of hernias involving the intestine are forgotten without the tissue, and this type of internal hernia is called "zirbal."
Some times it is caused by wind, and some times it occurs when the hernia splits open and remains unnoticed, causing grave danger for the patient, and sometimes it causes severe and painful complications, especially when pressure is applied.
In the treatment of this disease with spices, caution must be exercised to avoid the danger of poisoning in the process.
The method of operating on that hernia is to command the patient to push the intestine back into its cavity using their own hands until it returns, and then wrap a cloth around it between their buttocks, and lift their legs.
Then tie the cord that secures the scrotum at the opening, and cut through the entire scrotum; and then insert two fingers into the incision to divide the scrotum as needed.
And if the division of the scrotum is according to the quantity that you can comfortably avoid leaving any part unattended.
Then excise the tissue that is left behind after removing the scrotum, until the white hard mass of each division is exposed.
Then you insert your finger into the opening that exposes the white mass left behind from the scrotum, between the masses, and remove any adhesion in the area behind the testicle.
Then wrap the cord around the testicles at their openings, and with your left hand remove the white mass from each, and lift the testicle along with the white mass to the incision site; and command the assistant to stretch out the testicle beyond it, and you dissolve the adhesion behind it using a complete solution.
Search for any signs that there may not be a cause for the hernia being wrapped in the hard white mass. If you find a cause, then push it back into the abdomen.
Then make an incision on the remaining part of the scrotum where pus and blood will flow as we previously recommended.
Then apply wool soaked in oil to the wound and wait; then apply the recommended stitches (and sometimes the white mass is cauterized, which we mentioned earlier to prevent bleeding, as this often occurs), and leave the stitch until it falls out on its own.
If the danger persists, boil some water and soak a cloth in it, then apply it to the wound until it falls off as we previously said.
Take care of the wound with other methods for treating wounds until it heals.

In this hernia, there is no known effective treatment for it.

Title. LXVIII.

Title. LXIX.
On Castration.
Know that castration is forbidden in our law, but I mention it here because it is relevant to this book; and the reminder of it is only necessary in two cases: one is when the doctor asks about it because he knows its treatment when it occurs; the other reason is that we often need to perform castrations on animals for our use, such as horses, cows, pigs, and similar animals.
And so it is said that castration can be done in two ways: either through tearing or by making an incision.
But in the case of castration by tearing, the method for this operation is that we seize the animal by the testicles in warm water until they become softened and swollen and hang down. Then carefully take hold of them with your hand inside until they are resolved and do not appear again afterwards.
But in the case of castration by incision, it is necessary that you hold the animal and press the scrotum of the testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the spermatic cords and make an incision on each one to about two inches deep.
And then carefully remove the testicles, taking care not to damage them or the surrounding tissues. Do not leave any cause on those areas other than a thin thread, which is placed over the vessels.
The method of castration by tearing is better because it leaves less cause for the testicles to swell, thus the animal will not desire copulation.
And carefully treat the wound until it heals up.
Chapter LXX.
On the treatment of Hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in males occurs in two ways: the first is when a hole appears in the scrotum between the testicles, where there appears what resembles female labia.
And sometimes this condition also causes the testicles to expel urine from the scrotum.
But in females, it is a different case: where the female genitalia at the pubis resemble two testicles of a male, slightly smaller and located at the base of the penis, similar to the scrotum of a man and two testicles.
And the treatment is for three cases: two in males and one in females. It is necessary to make an incision in the affected areas and to remove the excretion that comes from it, and then treat those areas with other remedies for other wounds.
In the second case of males, where urine comes from the scrotum, there is neither treatment nor operation for it.
Chapter XXI.
On Lengthening and Swelling due to Female Causes.
Lengthening is a natural process that occurs when the vagina is stretched and becomes larger, following the natural regimen; but in some women it becomes exaggerated to such an extent that it spreads out like in men and enters the uterus.
Therefore, it is necessary to remove the excess of lengthening with your hand or a syringe and make an incision.
And do not deepen the incision, especially near the cervix, to avoid bleeding.
And treat that area with remedies until it heals up.
However, swelling is the flesh that grows within the abdomen of the mother before delivery, and it extends outward near the vaginal opening, similar to lengthening (and for this reason some people call it "postpartum disease"); therefore, it is necessary to make an incision in the same way as we do with lengthening, and treat it until it heals up.
Chapter LXXII.
On the treatment of Ulcers (or sores).
An ulcer is when the female genitalia is not pierced or torn in some way. It can be either natural or accidental.
Accidental is when the ulcer has previously been caused by disease, and that can be due to excess flesh or thin or thick thread.
It is caused either in the mother's perineum, her costal area, or the superficial or deep pus, and it is forbidden to have sexual intercourse, to engage in pregnancy, and to menstruate, and it is also forbidden to menstruate.
The recognition of the ulcer is done by the midwife, if the opening is visible, it should be sewn up with silk thread or ray; but if it is not visible, you should search for it with your fingers or with the rod (a medical instrument).
But if the opening is due to thin thread and is close to the two labia, you should catch it and tear it apart.
And place your fingers on both labia and indicate which one is the most swollen first.
The woman should be in the same position, with her legs apart and extended, and gently pull both labia until the thin thread is torn and the opening is exposed.
Apply wool, soak it in oil and place it on the affected area, and change it daily to ensure that the wound does not heal prematurely.

If the abscess is caused by an ulcerated wound, suspend it with an ointment, and then lance it.
And here are the medicines that stop bleeding without cutting, such as henbane, dragon's blood, and mastic resin, mixed with white wax.
Then administer a large leaden cannula to prevent the wound from healing too quickly.
Keep it for several days and apply hot compresses to it.
Then let it heal naturally with the other methods of treatment until it is healed.
Sometimes it happens during childbirth for other women's flesh, and then you must lance it according to this method. If it is an abscess with cancerous growths in the womb, do not oppose it with iron in any way.

The abdomen must be tightly bound on the right and left sides with ease.
If the mouth of the mother is narrowed, we have already recommended the cure through vomiting and with oil and herbs.
But if none of the causes that have been recommended are forgotten, then you must be careful not to overdo the extraction from her, but rather it is necessary that what has come out of her into the mouth of the mother should be placed in the female's cavity and covered with salve and a four-fold medication; for this will make her swell for about three days, then dissolve, and disappear.
But when she swells, the evil authority rises to the head and stomach, and afflicts the patient; therefore, something should be administered under fumigation and in accordance with this.
But one of the ancients has already spoken of a fumigation of garlic and dried figs.
The shape of the instrument with which the woman is fumigated should have the ability to retain menstruation and afterbirth:
It should be made of iron or of earth.
Then let the narrow part be placed in the cavity and the wide part above the fire, and the fumigation should be placed on the arms of the fire.
And let it contain within itself that which is consumed by the fumigation, and repeat another one.
Treatment for the anus of the unborn child.
Newborn infants and their anuses that are not perforated, which are soft and open. Therefore, the midwife must perforate the soft and open anus with a pointed instrument; otherwise, she should perforate it with a sharp spatula and ensure that she does not touch the rectum.
Then cover it with wool soaked in wine and oil, and treat it with salve inside until it is healed.
But if you fear that it may open again, then cover it with a tube for several days, and remove it when the child wants to relieve itself.
And there often occurs obstruction of the anus due to consolidation of a wound or abscess; therefore, that consolidation must be incised and treated with what has been said about treatment and lead.
Treatment for fistulas that have descended.
Fistulas that descend into the descents are often thick and swollen, which occur near the anus or in the space of one of the descents.
And it is a fistula or a boil.
And when the thickening is old and turns from the foul, white moisture or subtle pus, some of these fistulas may penetrate.
And those that penetrate are recognized by what is expelled from them through the opening and by swelling; some patients also experience expulsion, and often worms come out of these.
And some of these fistulas often penetrate into the space, penetrating into the bladder and into the meat of the scrotum; and some penetrate into the joint of the thigh and into the knot of the coccyx.
And what is known as a fistula penetrating into the anus and not penetrating, is that you insert your pointed instrument into the anus, and make a small incision in the fistula when there is no hardness.
But if there is hardness in that, then make a small incision with lead or horsehair into the fistula until you feel the incision or the hair in your instrument.
And if you do not feel any of this or do not experience any cause of expulsion, worms, or swelling, as we have said, then you should know that it is non-penetrating and you can proceed with the treatment.
When the fistula penetrates into the bladder or into the meat of the scrotum, its meaning is indeed of urine from that place and it should be forbidden until the location has been properly treated with medicine.
If the hernia penetrates into the joint of the thigh or into the bone and pain occurs in the vicinity, this is a sign that it will enter here if there is no treachery inside the bone, and pain in the vicinity of the injured area; that pus will appear quickly; that such treatment has no effect, nor can it be healed with ointment.
In all such fistulas there is not a cure, and the cure of these is the labor and futility of foolish doctors on which they are fixed.
But in one that is not penetrating and not old, healing with iron is hoped for as I shall advise you, and what I have tested.
It is that the patient lies between your hands on their back and raises their legs into the air, so that their hips are inclined towards their belly, and carefully insert a probe of lead or of iron if there is treachery in the fistula, until you know where it enters.
And if the patient feels pain around the neck, then you must insert your finger into the neck.
If you feel the probe already penetrating by itself, then what you should do is to insert your finger between the probe and that tissue or flesh, and then you will know with certainty that it is penetrating; and at that point, do not work on it, for there is no healing in that place, as we have said.
But others say that it heals in some men temporarily.
And of the medicine by which healing is hoped for in that place, it is that you ignite a subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been previously described, and insert it into the fistula until it reaches around the neck; then return it two or three times until you know that all the tissues adjusted by the fistula, which resemble the feather of a bird's quill, have been cauterized.
And cure that one with calves wrapped in bandages until they heal all the tissues that are adjusted, and cure that one with medicines that generate and consolidate flesh, and if it is healed, good; and if not, do not attempt healing by another method for a time.
And if the probe is inside, but does not penetrate into your rectum, which is covered with a membrane or with flesh, and sometimes the fistula is in that which dries up the surface of the scrotum, then you should dry the scrotum from the beginning of the fistula, and see if it dries up with the probe, and it should be in the fistula until the drying reaches the location where the tip of the probe emerges, and through the probe is freed and captured.
And cure those fistulated tissues that are similar to the canal of a bird's feather and leave no cause remaining in them.
And if blood flow sometimes comes between you and your action when you handle those tissues, then prepare a poultice and with a light instrument, cauterize it with fire or with sharp medicine, for cauterization with fire adjusts good habits: it is the adhesion of those tissues adjusted, and the abscess draining of the blood through drying of the humors.
And cure that one with calves wrapped in bandages or with crushed charcoal until the wound breaks open, and then cure the ulcer with hard-generated flesh ointment.
And these medicines have astringency and drying properties; when it is restored, it is healed and there will be no recurrence.
But if the fistula has already penetrated into the rectum and is elongated from the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the rectum and investigate with it.
And thus if the probe is covered with flesh or with tissue and is near penetration, then it is not an operation in that place but rather through trust and hope.
The cause is to administer it in one of three ways: either cauterize it as previously described; or to dry it until you achieve the concavity of the place so that it is possible for you to enter and cure it properly without tearing the ligament that contains the rectum, and be careful not to do so much drying that you tear the skin, and it may happen to the patient painlessly, without their will; or to elongate that covering and clean the pus that is dried near the rectum as previously described, either with a probe or another sharp instrument, and to clean those fistulated tissues in the area where you can do percrustation; and to force yourself to restore the entire ulcer through drying, and if the opening of the pus does not consolidate, and the fistula remains open in the lower part of the rectum, it will be easier for the patient. And sometimes the fistula is finished in this way: when you insert the probe into the fistula, it is at the side of the rectum near the surface of the body with the scrotum, and on the edge of the rectum, then take a probe with a perforated tip, which is similar to an awl for preparing the body as follows:
And enter into that faithful envelope of your five fields or around them; and carefully enter the fistula, try to reach its cavity until you succeed.

But if the orifices of the fistula are not penetrating, then you make them penetrate, in whatever way is prepared by you, but it must not be too deep, because it is not for you to do this so as not to injure the lacert; and carefully heal that into which it has been healed.
The method of spine splint for the splitting of the fistula: the curvature of which is sharp and the other end is not sharp, so that it does not penetrate unnecessarily, as sometimes happens.
Stitching hemorrhoids from which blood flows at the incision of those.
Hemorrhoids are of two kinds, for they can be like coal in the anus, or those are like fat from radishes. And those can be small and large, and blood flows from them constantly, and they are single, and they are moist, and they protrude out of the anus, and at their ends.
But those that protrude out of the anus are according to the dry months, from which clear water or a little blood with continuous flow comes, and according to the color of the skin.
And the healing of that which is inside the anus is that you command the patient to sit and express until the anus dries up and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Then you take hold of it with some tweezers or what you have those with your nail, and carefully cut the roots.
But if the tweezers are not available for those due to their humidity and softening of those, then take those with rough cloth or thread or woolen floss, and draw those out with your fingers, and carefully cut them and sprinkle some powdered herbs appropriate for cauterization at the incision, so that they are in place of cautery; or cauterize those as previously described in the chapter on cauterization. Then heal those with the other treatment until they are healed.
And if the anus does not obstruct evacuation, then cauterize the patient with a small bite in the area of the anus that should be moistened slightly, and the patient should gently press when necessary.
But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, the cause of them is slight, and you should take those with your nail or tweezers, cut them, and heal them as I said earlier until they are healed.
The one that you should incise, it is necessary to administer stitching of them according to this method: take the fistula and insert the needle into it and carefully draw out the hemorrhoids to the top, and make the needle penetrate through the other part, and envelop the two ends of the fistula on the side further away from the needle, lengthwise; and tie the hemorrhoid tightly, and do not bind the fistula and remove the needle.
And do this for all of them, leaving one loose and not sewing it up, so that the excess blood can flow from it.
Place a cushion on the anus with oil-soaked cotton or wax, and place that over the anus and command the patient to rest. Leave it until it is healed; when it is healed, heal those with salve or the other treatment until they are healed.
And since they are old and of no value in that medicine, it is necessary that you cut those with the point of a splint or your nail until they become moist and are prevented from consolidation; and heal those until they are consolidated.
Then remove those with the most violent reason, before they become dry and are scabbed over; and heal those until they are healed.

A wart is a small rough, round elevation on the surface of the body, and it is observed in many children.
The treatment for a wart is to extend and incise it, or to press it with a hot iron or with something that goes into the wound. If you want, cauterize this, as I said, with fire or with sharp medicine.
A bedbug is a small rough or large elevation on the surface of the body which moves around in the skin, and when it is touched, it feels like a bite from a bedbug, and it is found all over the body.
The treatment for a bedbug is to take a thin or blunt needle, and it should be strong, and place it on the bedbug inside its circle; then rotate your hand with the needle around the bedbug that you have enclosed within its circumference, and press it in the skin of the body, and eradicate the bedbug from its root.

The form of large and shallow incision:

The bag in which the urinary bladder or sheep's wool medicine is placed should be made of cowhide, and its size should be about a palm.
It should have holes pierced in it as it is rotated, and the size of the space between the holes should correspond to the thickness of a finger.
And insert it into the holes made with a pointed and sharp needle or around them; and adjust the bag to that hole; and when the bag is placed in it, it should be tight at the head of the needle between two distinguishing marks with strong pressure, and then cauterize each hole: However, the quality of cauterizing it is that you fill the bag with medicine, which is heated according to the tolerance of the patient; and make sure it is not too hot or too cold.
Place the patient on his back, and raise his legs and place a cushion under him or a lansol; then anoint the outside of the cautery with oil or albumen of egg or mucilage of fenugreek or similar substances; and insert it gently into the anus with ease, and have someone administer the bag and squeeze it forcefully and repeatedly until everything that is in the cauterizer is evacuated from the intestine; then remove the cauterizer and the patient lowers his legs to the wall.
And if the medicine is not enough in that case, have more of it; and if it remains there for an entire night, it is more beneficial later.
However, if you cauterize it in the cases of abdominal distention and its resolution, then you should continue inserting the cautery until it is healed.

Treatment of sores.
I have already said in the division of treating sores what is necessary for the free treatment, and I say again the treatment of those with more and with medicine according to the need.
Therefore, I say that sores are varied according to what causes the sores and according to the area where the sores occur.
And the causes of sores that are often caused by injuries such as stones, incisions of space or sword, blows with a lance, fist, spear, arrows, or similar things.
These plagues that are in the locations of the body are similar to a plague that settles on the head, neck, feet, belly, back, and are similar to those of the limbs.
And you recommend the treatment of some plagues by following that reasoning and rule for other plagues.
And you begin with the simple plagues of the head, because the composition will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore say that when a simple plague occurs in the head, and it is not a fracture, consider: if it is due to stone or something similar, and the patient has already tightened the bandage only, but there is a large wound and you fear that the patient may develop an abscess, then quickly lance the skull and do not delay; and extract it according to the amount of strength of the blood, unless any other reason prohibits phlebotomy, especially if the blood that has come out is little.
And ensure that phlebotomy is done opposite the affected side, and protect the patient from replenishment, food, and heavy food.
But if there is any reason for the minucium, then it should be reduced from food and avoid meat and wine.
And pause over the plague, if an abscess has formed, apply oil of roses or wine that is steeped in it.
But if it is certain that there is an abscess, then pause over the plague, if the patient's blood and air have not changed, apply the powder that I will recommend in small amounts.
But if the air has already changed, then pause over some salve until it is healed.
But if the plague is large or due to incision of space and similar things, and the lips are not properly aligned, then align them with suture as I will recommend for their suture.
But if the plague has exposed bone and cartilage without retention, but only a small suspension is used, then incise it and care for the wound with medicines and restore the skin to its place using bandages, and order the patient to eat food that is heavy and nourishing: meat and bread, until it is healed.
If the bandage becomes putrid and does not adhere to the bone, then you should incise it all and drain it, and care for it.
But if in these plagues there is an artery or vein from which blood flow may occur and it has not been separated by medicines, then you should inquire about the artery, and if it is not incised, you should incise it with a spatula, or tie it; and if necessity compels that what has been said does not conform, then cauterize it until blood flow is stopped.
And if these plagues are simple and small, then their cause is light; therefore you powder over them with this powder, because it solidifies before the air changes those.
And the method of the powder is as follows: prepare an oil made from one part of camphor, two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of non-extinct herbs; grind everything together and sieve it, and fill the plague with the powder, and tie it tightly with good binding until it adheres to the skin, and coagulate it with blood.
And keep it above with powder and release it only when it is healed, because the medicine has not yet been absorbed into it until it is healed.
And sometimes perform this caution alone when camphor and dragon's blood are not available to you.
And perform this method of operation on large plagues when it is necessary to pause over them and tighten them, and on new plagues with their blood, which the air has not yet changed.
But if the air has already changed, and especially in summertime, it is not intended to use this powder position, but rather care for them with what has been said, by pausing over them with some salve, or pausing over them with flour water and honey until they drain pus; and care for them with the other treatment until they are healed.
But if a fracture occurs in bone, and it is small, you should extract it with forceps.
I will heal the poisonous fractures of the head.
Of the ailments of the neck.
But if the ailment occurs in the neck, there is no difference in treatment, and the same medicine applies for the simple fracture of the head.
But if the nerves or artery in the neck have been cut, it is not advisable to treat it immediately with anything that causes violent stitching, such as ziniar and zegi (arsenic and vinegar), which are harmful to nerves and constrict them. And do not apply any ointment to the ailment that causes it to freeze, as the substance of nerves is cold and its continuity is with the brain, which is the most important part of all members.
And if it can be cured with light medicines such as washing it with sweet water, sometimes infused in rose oil or not, thuja (Thuja occidentalis) when washed with sweet water and other herbs mixed according to this method, and gargling with moist liquid.
But if the ailment is large, administer a stitch or sew the lips of it, and apply care with powder until it heals.
But if the ailment has depth or occurs in the lower part of the pustule, then pierce it at its most depressed location.
But if an artery has already been cut in the ailment and bleeding occurs, then separate it, tie it, or cauterize it if necessary.
But if the vertebrae of the cervical spine have already been cut, and the veins of the neck are saved, then you should sew the skin around the cervical spine with sutures on the spinal canal, without touching it; bend it to its natural shape, strengthen it with a suitable structure, and leave it for several days; apply care with astringents to reduce swelling and inflammation until it heals.
If the wound has already penetrated into the bone, then you should percuss it and if there are any fragments of bones, remove all that can be removed; and let what cannot be handled go in so that the wound may heal, and it should be separated and the swelling around it should be alleviated.
And if the wound is fresh, then you should sprinkle that powder which has been recommended over it. But if the wound becomes a fistula, you should treat it with what will come to mind in its appropriate chapter.
If the wound is from a lance or sword, and sometimes of great depth, you should consider whether there is wind coming from the wound if the patient complains about it; in this case, you should know that the wound is fatal.
And if there is no great depth in the wound and it is fresh with blood, you should wait for the first hour before applying powder, and avoid pressing too hard so as not to hold back the blood in the depth of the wound and allow it to return to the heart and alleviate the patient, but apply an attractive ointment to it, and remove it after two days.
And if there is no ointment available, you should wait for the orifice of the wound to become caked with old scab so that it may draw out the humidity; and have the patient sleep on the wound so that it may run what is in it.
But if three days or more have passed since the wound occurred and the patient has not experienced spasm, palpitations of the heart, tremors, or any other good conditions, you should know that the wound is healed; and then treat it with heat and other treatments until it is completely healed.
But if the healing of it is delayed and it is always open, you should know that a fistula has formed; treat it according to its appropriate chapter.
And if the wound is caused by a sword or knife, and is simple on the surface of the foot or back, you should treat it with sutures if it is large, or powder if it is small.
But if the wound has already penetrated into the bone and there are separate pieces of bone, you should turn the wound and try to extract those pieces. If the pieces of bone are not separated, you should let them go in so that the wound may heal and the removal of them is alleviated.
And the treatment for other accidental wounds in other parts of the body is the same as that which has been said.
Of abdominal wounds.
The condition of the abdomen that occurs can be large, small, or medium-sized.
Small disruptions are made with difficulty by another means, and it is known that the reduction of them is difficult if you do not take care to insert them into their proper place immediately, for it becomes swollen and thickened, making the insertion of them difficult.
Therefore, the best disruption is medium-sized, because in this case, the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, as it is with the two types mentioned above.
You should know that the suturing of the abdomen is done in four ways, but two of these are common and necessary for suturing other wounds on the body.
The remaining two sutures are specific to other wounds, but they are particularly suitable for the suturing of the abdomen.
And I recommend that you have exposure and dissection at your disposal.
Therefore, I say that when the wound is small and it has caused the intestine to protrude through it, making reduction difficult, you should do one of two things: either because of the smallness of the disruption as mentioned before, or when inflammation has come upon the intestine due to the coldness of the air.
And so when that is the case, you should warm the intestine by placing a sponge or damp cloth in hot water alone, or by putting it in warm water, camphor, cinnamon, and bandages around it to resolve the inflammation.
And sometimes you will find that it has stiffness, and water alone is better for the resolution of inflammation.
And so when inflammation is resolved, you should moisten the intestine with water that contains salt and pepper, as this helps to alleviate the difficulty of insertion.
But if insertion is difficult despite this treatment, you should make a small incision with an instrument and then remove the morbid matter.
The primary treatment is better if it is not dry and there is no need to let it dry out due to necessity or negligence.
Of the instrument, cut its shape:
The first part should be curved and sharp, the second part should not be pointed but rounded, the end should be fine, but not as thin as a needle point, it should be blunt to a small degree.
And since the wound is expanded and the intestine has come out, it is necessary to reduce it in its natural form, in its own proper place if possible, for it is better.
When the injury is widespread and located at the lower abdomen, you must make the patient lie on their back and raise their legs as high as possible; if it is above the abdomen, you must raise the head of the patient and their feet to the same level as the injured area.
If the injury is in one of the two parts of the abdomen, you must immediately focus and decide which side the wound is on so that the other side may be raised higher.
You must also treat large wounds and small wounds.
In small wounds, you should prepare what is needed, and make sure the assistant who will minister to the wound has it ready in your presence, holding the entire wound with their hand and adjusting the edges of it, and then carefully expose one part at a time for suturing, ensuring that no other obstacle interferes.
This is the common suturing method: take a needle or a large needle depending on the size of the wound; position it at the edge of the wound on the anular finger's tip and pull the needle through once, without piercing both ends of the thread, near the inside edges of the skin folds, until it penetrates that area; you have already added two ends of the thread and two ends of the suture, making four orders.
Then pull the thread through twice around the needle, and several times in both areas, and draw together the two edges and the wound by a proper suturing; then position the thickness of the finger and insert another needle into it, pulling it along with the first needle as before; do not stop until you have completed the entire contraction of the wound.
Needles should be neither too thick nor too thin, because thin needles penetrate the flesh lightly; while thick ones are difficult to insert into the skin, therefore it is necessary that they be moderately thin and thick.
The needle should not be inserted too deep into the adjacent skin, so that the flesh is not pierced lightly and the wound does not burst before it heals.
Do not prolong the suturing so that the wound does not hinder healing.
Draw the tips of the needles so as not to hurt the patient during their sleep and place a powder over the suture, covering all areas, which will hold the tips of the needles; leave it in place until you know that the wound has healed.
This method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it covers the suture with only one or two needles around it.
However, the second suturing method is common: you must administer four corners (two from the skin and two from the suture) in one go with a needle that is tightly wrapped in both thinness and thickness.
When the needle penetrates these four corners, retract the needle from that side of the starting area, to draw back the purulent material from the wound to the healthy part, so that the suture is like a sewn fabric where the cloth is strengthened.
Stop between each stitch the thickness of the finger tip.
This suture is known to men.
I sewed the wound that had occurred in a man's abdomen, who had been stabbed with a sword, and the size of the wound was greater than one palm, and it was located near two palms from the belly button of the middle part of the member; and after waiting for 24 hours for the intestine to come out of the wound, I reduced it.
The wound healed in the space of 15 days or thereabouts, and I cured him and he recovered; and he lived for many years and remained in his normal condition.
The other doctors had judged that he would not recover; and by a miracle, because I did not cure him with poultices, because there was no poultice or any medicine in that area, instead I placed cotton on the wound twice a day and washed it repeatedly with honey water until it healed.
However, I will describe two types of suturing as narrated in the word.
You should start with skin suturing, and insert the needle from the outside to the inside.
And thus, as the needle penetrates through the abdomen and in that place it is placed the thread according to the rule and in length of the entire body, leaving the end of the cipher where the needle was inserted; and make the other end of the needle penetrate from the inner part at the inner end of the hernia to the outer end of the incision on the other side of the midline.
And thus, as you have inserted it there, make it pass again through the other end of the hernia from the inner side to the outer side; and leave the end of the cipher that is in this location, and insert the needle in the other end of the incision from the inner side to the outer side.
Make your insertion pass through the hernia with which you have inserted into the abdomen, until it reaches the other side of the incision.
And bring it together from this side and connect the other end with the one in the abdomen that was penetrated, extract the needle from the hernia that was penetrated, return it to the abdomen, connect the other end of the hernia with the other incision, and remove that one from the abdomen.
Make it pass again and again, and make it pass again and again inside until you sew everything that is on the outside according to this example.
The sum of this suturing method is that you sew with a skin suture, the same one used to sew skins, unless you sew the hernia once from the side of the abdomen incision, and leave the other side open until it is completed.
However, the second type of suturing, which is commonly called Guadia, and this is said because it comes from there and is recommended, is that you sew it according to half-half, as some physicians do, unless all the parts are connected in a natural way; and they apply one end of the other to the other end, and that is done as I have suggested.
You must place the needle at your side of the incision, and make it pass through to the other side only, leaving two ends of the hernia; and turn the needle around and make it pass from outside to inside in the two ends of the hernia.
And turn each of them around, and make each one pass from the inside to the outside in two opposite directions.
And this method of suturing is better than the common light suture, and it is the suturing that precedes remembrance.
This is the Gaulish saying.
However, some say that the abdominal suture is corrected with two needles, so that you insert one needle in each of them and begin with the incision of the needle that is yours, and make it pass to the other side according to the suturing of those who sew the hearts together.
And you should know that when disruption is in the middle of the abdomen, the suture of it is more difficult than those of other parts of the abdomen.
However, the treatment for hernia is judged as that for other hernias.
The cause is that when you succeed in the hernia while it is still fresh before the air changes it, and you reduce the intestine and sew it up properly, then pause over the embrocation powder.
And if the air has already altered the hernia, then pause over some embrocation ointments that are present among you until they become hard and bind the hernia and the incision; and cure it in this way as is the treatment for other hernias until it is healed.
However, if you are not present with the medications, then pause over it immediately, because it begins to bleed, exude pus and change twice a day as you have shown me, until it is healed, for you do not need any other treatment in many cases when hernias are simple.
However, if you fear that the hernia may communicate with damage to the main members, it is necessary for you to immerse linen wool in boiled oil or raw oil, and apply it in the circuit of the areas between the joints and leave it until it cools.
And if there is pain or putrefaction in your hernia, which often goes unnoticed, you must sterilize it with black sticky vinegar, especially if the pus has spread in the hernia and makes an exit by penetrating into its cavity.
And you should know that a large hernia heals more slowly than a small hernia.

Oh son, beware that foolish doctors and the common people boast about this chapter, and those who for a time do not read the books of the ancients nor learn a single letter from them.
Therefore, this method of the learned men in our land is hidden; and I have not forgotten it for a time, but I have only applied what follows after prolonged reading of the books of the ancients and study on their understanding, until I extracted the science from them.
And direct it to experience and study in the course of my life.
And you have now described in this chapter all that concerns the main science and on which my experience has been passed; therefore, I have condensed it for you and relieved it of lengthy discussion; and I have summarized it at the end of summary; and shown it at the end of explanation; and formed many forms of the instruments used in it, as is done by adding explanation, just as I did in the two preceding chapters.
Chapter First.
Summary and collections from the essence of fractures in bones, from which it is necessary to make a preliminary explanation before we begin remembering the restoration of broken members and various others of each. Therefore, let me state in the prelude of this chapter the summary of the discourse; and the chapters to which it is necessary for the craftsman to devote himself and stand still on the truth of these, so that you and those who are prompt and can learn or understand this noble art from you.
And therefore I say that when a fracture, dislocation, twist, or break occurs, it is necessary at the beginning to apply phlebotomy or leeching to it, or whatever else is not prohibited by any reason, such as weakness of virtue, or if it happens in an invalid, or in old age, or during hot weather, or during cold.
And let it be provided with food consisting of grassy herbs and meats of birds and crabs; and forbid large meats and fill them if they are filled with food and any food that fills the veins with blood, unless you are sure of a cauterized abscess, and if you fear effusion of matter in the member.
And then return the patient to his primary regimen according to his usual custom.
And since the broken bone begins to be restored, it is necessary that the patient be fed with nutritive foods consisting of dense and heavy nourishment in which there is viscosity, such as food made from cooked wheat flour and water, rice, cabbage, peas, beef, fresh fish, thick milk, eggs, and similar foods, and on this diet coagulation of the fracture occurs more easily.
And you should know that the bones broken in men who are in the prime of life and in old age cannot be continued and consolidated according to their nature due to the drying out of the members.
But nature adjusts and connects some cause similar to glue in the broken bone of every part, which causes swelling that adheres to it until it is consolidated and hardened together, until the end of growth and firmness comes, such as fire at the beginning, unless you prohibit this from its work.
And for this reason it is necessary to stop the food of the patient, food that is heavy and viscous and dense, as we have said.
And you should know that the types of fractures are diverse according to the diversity of the members, because a fracture in the bone of the thigh is different from a fracture in the bone of the head; and the fracture of the bone of the foot is different from the fracture of the bone of the hand; and similarly all other members are different from each other.
And I will proceed with the memory of every type of fracture, explained in its separate chapter.
Diversity of fractures within itself. And the types of fractures in bones are diversified within themselves; because a curved fracture is different from one that occurs at the stars, and some are fractures according to the length of the bone: and these are the fractures of the tibia and shinbone and those that occur without or with addition, such as the one prepared for writing, and is a fracture with a wound and disruption in the head, and is a fissure fracture.
And in all cases it is an engine or torment specifically in the restoration of him, according to his recall of himself in distinct locations.
A movable splint for a bone fracture. A fractured bone is recognized by its deformity, and from this projection and perception of it in sensation, and from this when you compress it with your hand.
Therefore, if there is no deformity apparent or it does not hurt when touched with movement of the bone and the patient does not experience great pain, then it is not a fracture here.
It is possible that there is a deformity or small fissure, in which case you must press it with your hand and compress all of it; pause over the medicine that comes to mind at that moment suitable for the location; and apply narrowly with subtle compression.
And know that the place which is arched and not split in two or otherwise that does not happen in the stagnation, such as the entire part of its circumference, then it is necessary to begin from your time with the rectification of it, having applied an abscess cauterization.

Apply strength according to the recall of it.
